<div id="review_1124236345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1124236345" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1124236345?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fanboy-goes-squee">fanboy-goes-squee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1124236345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4970716325872410889">Re-read 12/17/17<br/><br/>I didn't dislike this novel any on a re-read. Indeed, knowing what's going to occur in the next novel actually improved the overall plot for me. <br/><br/>I originally came to the conclusion that most of the historical plots were relatively inconsequential. After all, aren't we playing tourists with the time-travel bits? But no. The plots and the carry-through with a large cast of characters both vampire and other feels entirely justified on the re-read. <br/><br/>Other than that, I pretty much sque</span>
  <span id="freeText4970716325872410889" style="display:none">Re-read 12/17/17<br /><br />I didn't dislike this novel any on a re-read. Indeed, knowing what's going to occur in the next novel actually improved the overall plot for me. <br /><br />I originally came to the conclusion that most of the historical plots were relatively inconsequential. After all, aren't we playing tourists with the time-travel bits? But no. The plots and the carry-through with a large cast of characters both vampire and other feels entirely justified on the re-read. <br /><br />Other than that, I pretty much squeed all over again because of the mightily researched and loved past of 1590. Add a ton of real personages and give them so much life and verve and it feels like I just nerded out.<br /><br />And the straight UF experience is only enhanced. :)<br /><br />Oh, and let's be honest here. It's a romance. No matter how I try to deny it, it's all romance. :)<br /><br /><br />Original Review:<br /><br />The inner English Lit fanboy in me went squee many times as I read this one. I was teased and thrilled and thoroughly amused by being plopped into Elisabeth's England and Austria and France, meeting all of the fascinating characters of the time. Shakespeare was always an inconsequential flop in the background and Kit was suddenly thrust into the limelight like I thought he always ought to have been. <br /><br />The novel took a sharp turn from urban fantasy into historical fantasy, rich and detailed and a pure delight to behold. And yet, we all know language is always going to be a problem so I didn't really mind that late middle English was seamlessly translated into the modern English. It allows us the joy without any of the hardships. Indeed, the whole novel was some of the easiest complicated tales I've ever had the pleasure of staying up all night to read. I loved the first novel, but this one tickled a lot of fancy bones for me.<br /><br />The plot in this or the previous novel is relatively inconsequential. The people are much more important, and the care and detail put into them is pure magic. Of course, magic is fun while the stormclouds slowly encroach upon the sunny day, but we can feel the raindrops forming and the time for preparation is slipping away.<br /><br />I'm a big fan of this novel. Magic isn't much of a crutch, but the developments are enough to push the reader through a few of the snags. That being said, I had a great time reading it and have no regrets about the directions it has taken. I'm thoroughly invested.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4970716325872410889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7025097464747151356">As soon as I finished A Discovery of Witches, I immediately went online to find out when I should expect the sequel. It was a long wait, but completely worth it. Harkness' view of Elizabethan London and Europe is just awesome, and the trip to Prague was an added bonus that I had not expected. Not only did the plot line get more compelling, but Harkness was also able to weave in the difficulties of the newly wed. I savored every minute of this novel, and I can hardly wait to get it on audio.<br/><br/>Audio</span>
  <span id="freeText7025097464747151356" style="display:none">As soon as I finished A Discovery of Witches, I immediately went online to find out when I should expect the sequel. It was a long wait, but completely worth it. Harkness' view of Elizabethan London and Europe is just awesome, and the trip to Prague was an added bonus that I had not expected. Not only did the plot line get more compelling, but Harkness was also able to weave in the difficulties of the newly wed. I savored every minute of this novel, and I can hardly wait to get it on audio.<br /><br />Audio was just outstanding and I think I will be a freak and listen to it again sooner rather than later :)</span>

<div id="review_351537402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351537402" />
    <a title="Karen Ng" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/251567-karen-ng"><img alt="Karen Ng" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444188199p2/251567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351537402?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Ng" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Ng" href="/user/show/251567-karen-ng">Karen Ng</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251567-karen-ng?shelf=travel">travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251567-karen-ng?shelf=medical">medical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251567-karen-ng?shelf=europe">europe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251567-karen-ng?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251567-karen-ng?shelf=copy-received-for-review">copy-received-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251567-karen-ng?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251567-karen-ng?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251567-karen-ng?shelf=parallel-universes">parallel-universes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351537402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer986008025860869628">Every so often, a book comes along. It’s everything you imagine a great fiction to be. It evokes the tremendous joy of just being able to read, to immerse yourself in a book so fully, to jump into a journey where every sense in your body is heightened, and your mind stimulated. Then the last page is turned, you sigh with sadness since you know you will not be able to find another book like this for a long, long time. <br/><br/><b>Shadow of Night is such a book.</b><br/><br/>I wrote these in my review of the first book of </span>
  <span id="freeText986008025860869628" style="display:none">Every so often, a book comes along. It’s everything you imagine a great fiction to be. It evokes the tremendous joy of just being able to read, to immerse yourself in a book so fully, to jump into a journey where every sense in your body is heightened, and your mind stimulated. Then the last page is turned, you sigh with sadness since you know you will not be able to find another book like this for a long, long time. <br /><br /><b>Shadow of Night is such a book.</b><br /><br />I wrote these in my review of the first book of the trilogy:<br /><br /><i> “The author has in depth knowledge not only about history, but also science, architecture, Europe, culinary delights and wine… The book immediately reminded me of "The Historian" by Elizabeth Kostova, since both story took me to places in Europe that I've never been and historical periods that were so enlightening…..The story will be a delight for people who actually enjoy accurate scientific, historical, culinary and geographical information. The author has a wealth of knowledge and a unique style of writing and she's willing to share.”</i><br /><br />The review still rings true for the second installment, and more so. For readers who disliked the first installment of the series due to the slowness of the beginning, you’ll be delighted to hear that this book started right at the part where the first book dropped off, and is a thrill ride all the way to the end. You can also find satisfactory answers to most, if not all the burning questions that you had after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8667848.A_Discovery_of_Witches__All_Souls_Trilogy___1_" title="A Discovery of Witches (All Souls Trilogy, #1) by Deborah Harkness" rel="nofollow noopener">A Discovery of Witches</a>. I know it’s a gruesome wait for the second book in the series, but the wait is well worth it…this book surpassed everything I had imagined it to be.<br /><br />The story begins right where the first book left off, Matthew and Diana landed in Elizabethan England, 1590, hoping to find the enchanted Ashmole 782, as well as someone to help the spellbound Diana to learn her abilities. You’ll be surprised to encounter real historical characters that came alive under Harkness’ pen. Harkness’ take on Christopher Marlowe, Elizabeth I, Walter Raleigh and others were unique and creative, yet totally believable. I wrote in my review of ADoW how I fell in love with all the characters in the first book, yet I’m equally invested in all the new characters in Shadow of Night, both historical and fictional. It’s heartbroken to realize that these characters live in another space and time, and the only way I could reconnect with them is through the re-reading of this book.<br /><br />If you loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8667848.A_Discovery_of_Witches__All_Souls_Trilogy___1_" title="A Discovery of Witches (All Souls Trilogy, #1) by Deborah Harkness" rel="nofollow noopener">A Discovery of Witches</a> because of Harkness’ extensive and detailed descriptions of everything, you’re in for another treat. Harkness bought Elizabethan England to life using her professional knowledge and her unique writing voice: fashion, writing, architecture, food, music, writing, cooking, art, jewelries, home decors, smell of spices, and even the sound of church bells…. Be prepared to be immersed into 1600 Europe, from England to France and Prague, whether if you’re prepared or not. I recommend you to drop or finish every other book in your list to get ready for the most sensual ride in your life.<br /><br />I also love how Harkness incorporated a short chapter of the present after each part of the book. It shows how Diana and Matthew’s interference with the past affects the future. Everything that we do or not do has an impact in future, especially in our loved one and family’s life. Hopefully, history is valued and lessons learned. These chapters showed us how important it is to seize the moment and live your life, because there’s no going back. A few tender moments bought tears to my eyes. Compared to ADoW, the second book is much more emotional.<br /><br />Romance. Matthew and Diana in the 1600s were not without their problems. Matthew in Elizabethan era was a much more complex and dark character. The society was also less friendly for females, especially a witch with a weird accent. However, fans looking forward to more romance between them will not be disappointed. There are lots and lots of tender moments and love. It made up for what was lacking in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8667848.A_Discovery_of_Witches__All_Souls_Trilogy___1_" title="A Discovery of Witches (All Souls Trilogy, #1) by Deborah Harkness" rel="nofollow noopener">A Discovery of Witches</a>.<br /><br />If I write anymore here, this review will become a book! I do have a few recommendations before you jump in for the journey of your life: 1) Read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8667848.A_Discovery_of_Witches__All_Souls_Trilogy___1_" title="A Discovery of Witches (All Souls Trilogy, #1) by Deborah Harkness" rel="nofollow noopener">A Discovery of Witches</a> first. There’s no way you could understand the plot and all the complexity of this book if you don’t know the history of the characters. 2) Many new characters are introduced in this book. Use the appendix/Guide at the end of the book to familiar yourself with them. They are divided by location, quite clever. 3) If you are going to look for a simple, easy read for entertainment, this book is not for you; but if you love history, science, Europe, art, literature, geography, religion, philosophy, (food and wine for ADoW)…then, get this book (and the first).<br /> <br />(Thanks for Penguin Group for allowing me to access an advance ebook for review through NetGalley. This book will be published on July 10, 2012)</span>
  <a data-text-id="986008025860869628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16942449427984161018">My Diana and Matthew:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402254148i/9912957._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Wow, what a sophisticated and remarkable story! Shadow of Night was like nothing I have ever read before and it surpassed all my expectations. This book offers the most amazing mixture of romance, history, paranormal and action. It was equally good (if not better) as first book and I enjoyed reading this book immensely.</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402254148i/9912958._SY540_.jpg' width='340' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/>Shadow of Night is that kind of book which you cannot put down because you need to know how things are going to end up. Simultaneously, you are trying to </span>
  <span id="freeText16942449427984161018" style="display:none">My Diana and Matthew:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402254148i/9912957._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Wow, what a sophisticated and remarkable story! Shadow of Night was like nothing I have ever read before and it surpassed all my expectations. This book offers the most amazing mixture of romance, history, paranormal and action. It was equally good (if not better) as first book and I enjoyed reading this book immensely.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402254148i/9912958._SY540_.jpg" width="340" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Shadow of Night is that kind of book which you cannot put down because you need to know how things are going to end up. Simultaneously, you are trying to read it slowly because you never want to finish it. <br><br>Shadow of Night is eventful book, there is no single boring part since something is happening all the time. It was really fascinating to read about Diana's encouters with famous historical figures and her attempts to merge into world in 1590. And while first half of the book was interesting, second half was absolutely exciting and thrilling because of all that magical things Diana learnt about herself.<br><blockquote>
  <i>"But it is the stone that best captures who you are: bright on the surface, fiery within and impossible to break."</i>
</blockquote><br>This book is full of new characters which I grew fond of immediately. Especially the Matthew's father and nephew. What is it about the men from de Clairmont family? It is impossible to resist them. Matthew in particular! And the bond that Diana and Matthew developed in this book was so beautiful and it made their relationship perfect in my eyes.<br><br>Shadow of Night answered plenty of questions about Diana's magical powers, Ashmole 782 manuscript and de Clairmont family. But one questions remained unanswered - how I am going to handle the waiting for the final book?<br><blockquote>
  <i>"“Philippe told me that mating was destiny. Once I found you, there would be nothing to do but accept fate’s decision. But that’s not how it works at all. In every moment, for the rest of my life, I will be choosing you—over my father, over my own self-interest, even over the de Clermont family.”"</i>

<div id="review_1309885310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1309885310?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1309885310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9076151877175047094"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com'>www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>I'm not even sure where to begin. I didn't like this book as much as the first one. I loved the first one! I'm not sure what happened... my mood..the book itself. I do believe the last book in the trilogy will be as good as the first and I can't wait to read it. <br/><br/>There were so many people in this book, but the author listed in the back of the book who everyone was in case you got lost. Some of the things seemed to drag on but I can see where the author needed t</span>
  <span id="freeText9076151877175047094" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com">www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br><br>I'm not even sure where to begin. I didn't like this book as much as the first one. I loved the first one! I'm not sure what happened... my mood..the book itself. I do believe the last book in the trilogy will be as good as the first and I can't wait to read it. <br><br>There were so many people in this book, but the author listed in the back of the book who everyone was in case you got lost. Some of the things seemed to drag on but I can see where the author needed to add so much information. I didn't mind that one in the first one, but I still can't put my finger on what went wrong with this book. <br><br>On that note, I did love a lot of the book. I loved the ending the most!! I don't want to add a spoiler but I am so excited to see what's going to come of this new predicament! <br><br>I enjoyed meeting Diana and Matthew's fathers in this book. That was a mild spoiler, but your going back to the past so what do you expect :) <br><br>Diana learns some different things about herself and Matthew for that matter. I absolutely loved her firedrake! <br><br>They didn't really get what they set out to do, but they did learn a lot of things. <br><br>I loved that Diana didn't really put up with much of anyone's crap in the book. Matthew on the other hand was different. He wasn't a force to be reckoned with, he was just there. I'm not sure if it was the time, his father, or what, but he came to his senses as the book got closer to the end. <br><br>I sooooo wish I could mention the end but I know there are some people that haven't read it so I will keep that to myself :) <br><br>I would rate this book on my feelings right now as a 3.5. It makes me feel like I'm letting Diana and Matthew down. Yes, I get into my characters! Don't judge me :) <br><br>I look forward to The Book of Life! <br><br><a href="http://s1379.photobucket.com/user/melmartD11/media/Signature_zpsuuzsi0pt.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436819219i/15507623._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo Signature_zpsuuzsi0pt.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_263760916" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/263760916" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2871271-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1258152693p2/2871271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/263760916?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/2871271-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=mindless-indulgence">mindless-indulgence</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=frustration-inducing">frustration-inducing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=brings-the-feminist-rage">brings-the-feminist-rage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer263760916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8692090232024246744"><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Historical detail & slow pace drags down sequel</i>
</b><br/><br/>Though I had a rocky experience with Harkness' first novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8667848.A_Discovery_of_Witches__All_Souls_Trilogy___1_' title='A Discovery of Witches (All Souls Trilogy, #1) by Deborah Harkness' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Discovery of Witches</a>, I began reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11559200.Shadow_of_Night__All_Souls_Trilogy___2_' title='Shadow of Night (All Souls Trilogy, #2) by Deborah Harkness' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadow of Night</a> with hopes that its setting in the past would add intrigue and excitement to the unfolding story. Unfortunately, it did not, and the story became more plodding and convoluted in this installment.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11559200.Shadow_of_Night__All_Souls_Trilogy___2_' title='Shadow of Night (All Souls Trilogy, #2) by Deborah Harkness' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadow of Night</a> suffered most from its almost obsession-like focus on detailing every aspect of the historical period in which it was set.</span>
  <span id="freeText8692090232024246744" style="display:none"><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Historical detail &amp; slow pace drags down sequel</i>
</b><br /><br />Though I had a rocky experience with Harkness' first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8667848.A_Discovery_of_Witches__All_Souls_Trilogy___1_" title="A Discovery of Witches (All Souls Trilogy, #1) by Deborah Harkness" rel="nofollow noopener">A Discovery of Witches</a>, I began reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11559200.Shadow_of_Night__All_Souls_Trilogy___2_" title="Shadow of Night (All Souls Trilogy, #2) by Deborah Harkness" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow of Night</a> with hopes that its setting in the past would add intrigue and excitement to the unfolding story. Unfortunately, it did not, and the story became more plodding and convoluted in this installment.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11559200.Shadow_of_Night__All_Souls_Trilogy___2_" title="Shadow of Night (All Souls Trilogy, #2) by Deborah Harkness" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow of Night</a> suffered most from its almost obsession-like focus on detailing every aspect of the historical period in which it was set. From particulars about the floor coverings to the convenient inclusion of almost every notable figure of the time, I felt bogged down in the details and the name-dropping. Character development also progressed in fits and spurts and ultimately stalled. Though Matthew and Diana have some "breakthrough" moments in their relationship, Diana remains relatively incompetent and reckless and Matthew continues to be controlling and possessive. Slow pacing made the first 80% of the novel drag, and very little time or attention was given to the threats or worries of the present day. When action or plot movement did occur, it provided little tension or excitement. The couple's impetus to be in the past - to hone Diana's magic and to find Ashmole 782 - often got lost among historical notes and unrelated intrigue. The mythology regarding time travel and Diana's magical skills was also unclear and seemed to contradict itself at times.<br /><br />Even though <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11559200.Shadow_of_Night__All_Souls_Trilogy___2_" title="Shadow of Night (All Souls Trilogy, #2) by Deborah Harkness" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow of Night</a> didn't work for me, this book might be an enjoyable read for those who love history and detail. The time spent exploring Diana's magic and her special capabilities was interesting, as was the information revealed toward the end of the novel about Ashmole 782 and its related prophecy; I finished the book wanting to know more about each. The story also provided some insight into Matthew's character and how his past and his family had shaped him. Chapters set in the present day that were interspersed between sections also provided glimpses into what was happening in the present-day world and moved things along for the secondary characters. Of all of the different parts in the book, I enjoyed these infrequent additions the most.<br /><br />While I can appreciate the ambitious nature of Harkness' series, I left this second book of the trilogy feeling unmoved again by the story or its characters. Even such, I will likely read the final installment when it comes out to see what happens to Diana, Matthew, and all those connected by Ashmole 782. As she wraps up her story, I hope that Harkness provides readers with faster pacing, clearer world building, and more character development.<br /><br />Note: This review refers to an advance review copy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8692090232024246744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2449477258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2449477258" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2449477258?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780755384754" href="/book/show/17270883-shadow-of-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2449477258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3862756731986064022">Buddy read with <b>Ruthie</b><br/><br/>Shadow of Night was a disappointment, it hurts because I have low expectations for this book, this book would have been better if it was 150-200 pages shorter.<br/><br/>This book started just where <i> A discovery of Witches</i> ended with Matthew and Diana travelling to the past, the year 1590. The writing is fun in some parts and other times boring and repetitive.<br/><br/>Even though this book this book is written in Diana a female's POV, this book is not diverse, the romance was cool, I love the </span>
  <span id="freeText3862756731986064022" style="display:none">Buddy read with <b>Ruthie</b><br /><br />Shadow of Night was a disappointment, it hurts because I have low expectations for this book, this book would have been better if it was 150-200 pages shorter.<br /><br />This book started just where <i> A discovery of Witches</i> ended with Matthew and Diana travelling to the past, the year 1590. The writing is fun in some parts and other times boring and repetitive.<br /><br />Even though this book this book is written in Diana a female's POV, this book is not diverse, the romance was cool, I love the world building, it's one of my highlights of this book. <br /><br />Diana was annoying and naive in most part of the book and other times she was fun. The worst part was that she acts like a child most of the time, she's 33 years old, a grown adult woman. Her relationship with Matthew had a lot of rocky parts in this book, the Matthew of the 16th century is different from the one she knows.<br /><br />Matthew was equal part cool and equal part annoying, he lost himself in that century. Matthew's multiple secrets and lives made their visit into the past harder than it ought to be.<br /><br />Jack an eight years boy is my favourite character in this book. I just wish the author invested more in his character. This part broke my heart.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Master Roydon?” Jack sidled closer to Matthew. His chin was trembling. Matthew’s hand shot out and grabbed him by the collar, stopping him before he could get too close to me. Jack didn’t flinch. “Are you having a nightmare?”<br />Matthew’s hand dropped, releasing the boy.. “Yes, Jack. A terrible nightmare.”<br />Jack slid his hand into Matthew’s. “I will wait by your side until it passes.” My eyes pricked with tears.</i>
</b><br /><br />Gallowglass is another cool character that I can't wait to meet in the 21st century. He is Matthew's vampire nephew.<br /><br />The school of night is cool, I like Matthew's friends. Philippe was a character I did not expect to like, he's such a smart and intelligent man who loves his family.<br /><br />The plan was to go to 1590, find someone to teach Diana how her magic works and find Ashmole 782. The plan has way too many holes, they didn't anticipate the troubles that they found. Most due to Matthew's arrogance and a few Diana's naivety. They spent seven months in the past which is not good at all.</span>

<div id="review_190672360" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190672360" />
    <a title="☕️Kimberly  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5082615-kimberly"><img alt="☕️Kimberly  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577559843p2/5082615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190672360?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☕️Kimberly  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="☕️Kimberly  " href="/user/show/5082615-kimberly">☕️Kimberly  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190672360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9345740649209922935">The tale literally picks up right where Discovery of Witches left off. Diana and Matthew find themselves landing back in Elizabethan London. Diana is thrilled to be able to visit a period she has studied but finds herself woefully unprepared. She quickly realizes that even with her education she is completely out of her element. From her speech to her mannerism it is obvious to all; she isn’t from around here. With the aid of Matthew’s eccentric friends, they will work to assist Diana with these</span>
  <span id="freeText9345740649209922935" style="display:none">The tale literally picks up right where Discovery of Witches left off. Diana and Matthew find themselves landing back in Elizabethan London. Diana is thrilled to be able to visit a period she has studied but finds herself woefully unprepared. She quickly realizes that even with her education she is completely out of her element. From her speech to her mannerism it is obvious to all; she isn’t from around here. With the aid of Matthew’s eccentric friends, they will work to assist Diana with these skills, secure a witch to train her and find the lost copy of Asmole 782. The tale that unfolds is absolutely breathtaking, filled with suspense, romance, danger and iconic characters throughout Elizabethan history.<br /><br />The characters in the All Souls Trilogy are flawed, fleshed out and I absolutely adore them. Diana finds herself out of her element. Her witchcraft is acting all sorts of bonkers. She is living in a time when witches are burned at the stake, the clothes are barbaric and women have no rights. In this novel we get to see tremendous growth in Diana. Her love and understanding of Matthew grows. She becomes more confident in her own skin and continues to be loyal, fearless and stubborn. I loved watching her discover her talents as a witch. This provides both funny and frightening scenes as her inability to control them creates mayhem. Then of course there is Matthew *swoons*. In this novel we learn so much about him and what has molded the modern day version. His history is both fascinating and sad. We get to see a darker side of Matthew as he confronts his past. He loves Diana but things are holding him back. I loved discovering his inner-workings. Diana peeled back his layers, bringing them closer together. The soft, tender side of Matthew was beautiful. There are a few flash forwards to present time and the characters we love. This provides insight into how Matthew and Diana are changing the future. We spend most of the novel in the years 1590 and 1591. This affords us the opportunity to witness history, attend the queen, and meet many historical characters. Harkness did a fantastic job of weaving them in the tale and giving them voice. I adored getting to know Gallowglass and Matthew’s father. The Queen and other characters gave me the chills and I feared for Diana. <br /><br />Harkness has an incredible gift for world-building. She brought the Elizabethan era to life. Her interpretation of the queen, the atmosphere, and the smells of London lifted the tale right from the pages and I become completely immersed. It is immediately evident that a tremendous amount of research went into writing this novel. I was delighted by the historical accuracy and believability. From the buildings, merchants and furnishing, Harkness's imagery was enthralling. The characters she introduced were fleshed-out, and my feelings toward them reflected that. Shadow of Night held my attention and kept me up late two evening in a row, but it was worth every sleep-deprived minute. Harkness spun twists and turns into the plot that completely captivating me. We travel all over Europe and I loved all the little details. The fear of discovery and the atmosphere of the times, especially towards witches made this tale very suspenseful. The romance between Diana and Matthew was genuine and beautifully portrayed. There was coupling and it was done beautifully. Even the most delicate reader won’t be offended. Watching their growth as a couple kept me spellbound. Together they share loss, love, fear, jealousy and a binding that will last forever. I found myself completely invested in their story. While I am once again drooling for the next book, it is also bittersweet for me. The knowledge that its publishing will bring this tale to an end is a sad one. I am not yet ready to let go of Matthew and Diana. While it did not end on a huge cliffhanger you are left knowing things are developing and this tale is far from over. <br />I want to thank Viking/Penguin publishing for providing this finished copy in exchange for my unbiased review.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9345740649209922935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2220193671" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2220193671" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2220193671?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/15769863-shadow-of-night">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2220193671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1489877906334552718"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515430079i/24859025.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/>This is the second book in the <i>All Souls</i> trilogy and mostly takes place in 1590/1591 after Diana and Matthew have time-walked there to be safe from the congregation, find the manuscript of Ashmole 782, as well as a witch capable of teaching Diana about her strange magic.<br/>It is thus that we meet characters like Walter Raleigh, Christopher Marlowe, Elizabeth I and even Matthew's father Philippe, who has quickly become my favourite character (along with Matt's nephew Gallowglass).<br/>The book takes </span>
  <span id="freeText1489877906334552718" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515430079i/24859025.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>This is the second book in the <i>All Souls</i> trilogy and mostly takes place in 1590/1591 after Diana and Matthew have time-walked there to be safe from the congregation, find the manuscript of Ashmole 782, as well as a witch capable of teaching Diana about her strange magic.<br>It is thus that we meet characters like Walter Raleigh, Christopher Marlowe, Elizabeth I and even Matthew's father Philippe, who has quickly become my favourite character (along with Matt's nephew Gallowglass).<br>The book takes place in London (Blackfriars), France (Sept-Tours), and Prague - as well as some modern places few and far between.<br><br>Once again, it is remarkable how much research has gone into the authenticity of the settings and Deborah Harkness has brought all the places to life in an uncanny way. I liked especially how she acknowledged and therefore incorporated the difficulties a time-traveller would definitely have to face, no matter how many history books one might have read. Too often in fiction people just travel back, wear the right clothes and all is well. Here, even the vampire who has lived through these times before has difficulties, let alone his modern-day wife, which only made the frame of the story more realistic.<br><br>It's therefore also no surprise that many things go wrong and it is once again friends and family Diana and Matthew have to rely on in order to survive - a theme already established in the first book that I adore as it also means the family you make, not just blood relatives.<br>It emphasized the point that history is not an exact science (no matter how much Diana would like it - and magic - to be just that) but rather one day after another just as in our lives and that the two protagonists have to improvise in order to get what they want and need. It's a process that makes them both learn about themselves as much as the world they live in and there are some sneaky similarities to the scientific mystery they are trying to solve.<br><br>One of my absolute favourite bits about this book was Goody Alsop and the coven of witches she assembled and how they taught Diana - so atmospheric, giving the reader this warm and comfy feeling! Just like Philippe did in his time's version of Sept-Tours! I really love that man.<br>The other thing I've come to really appreciate is the author's love for details. While the German dialogues (spoken at the court of the Emperor in Prague) were atrocious and the Spanish weren't much better (which made me wonder about the Latin bits - I really wish I had had Latin in school), there are many details added through the names of places or people such as the falcon named Šárka after a folklore character or Gallowglass having been an order of mostly Scottish mercenaries between the 13th and 16th century that lend their name to one of the best characters here because of that character's roots and personality. Even Peter Stubbe made an appearance through a newspaper article!<br><br>There is certainly heartship in here such as <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the constant betrayal by supposed friends or Diana's miscarriage of the first child - most of all, though, Philippe's certain death shook me - <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and I expect there to be at least as much in the next book, but there are light and funny moments in here as well. These moments being so pronounced because every single character, main and secondary, is fully fleshed out and distinctive.<br><br>It might have taken me a while to read this but that is in no way the book's fault. While it is quite thick and dense with information and events, it is never boring and the audio version was, once again, very good.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1489877906334552718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8096565945385147483" style="display:none">I FINALLY finished this darn book - thank heavens. It was a struggle and I was so disappointed. It was OK in the very beginning, then got totally lost in all of the non-directional padding and finally had some of the earlier pizzazz in the last 10 pages. <div id="review_240635202" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240635202" />
    <a title="Angela Cone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5421252-angela-cone"><img alt="Angela Cone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309962549p2/5421252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240635202?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela Cone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela Cone" href="/user/show/5421252-angela-cone">Angela Cone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240635202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14747937951682324143">If you were infatuated with A Discovery of Witches (and if you weren't I seriously wonder about you), you will be head over heels in love with Shadow of Night. SON picks up right where ADOW left off with Matthew and Diana landing in Elizabethan times (1590s). Diana is shocked when she learns that Matthew, who goes by Matthew Roydon in this time period, was a player in the elusive School of Night (Marlow, Raleigh, Chapman, Harriott) as well as friend to Shakespeare. Diana has quite a time trying </span>
  <span id="freeText14747937951682324143" style="display:none">If you were infatuated with A Discovery of Witches (and if you weren't I seriously wonder about you), you will be head over heels in love with Shadow of Night. SON picks up right where ADOW left off with Matthew and Diana landing in Elizabethan times (1590s). Diana is shocked when she learns that Matthew, who goes by Matthew Roydon in this time period, was a player in the elusive School of Night (Marlow, Raleigh, Chapman, Harriott) as well as friend to Shakespeare. Diana has quite a time trying to learn the speech patterns and vocabulary of the time as well as getting used to the itchy clothing. But perhaps Diana's biggest surprise is when she learns that Matthew is a spy for the Queen.<br /><br />While Diana is busy learning how to actually live in a time that she has very intimately studied, Matthew is trying to reacquaint himself with Elizabethan Mathew and at times that is complicated. But he does not lose focus on why they time walked and seeks to find Diana a tutor to learn how to harness her magic. Since this is a time period in which those expected to be witches are persecuted - painfully - they must be careful in attempting to seek another witch to train her.<br /><br />Matthew and Diana also continue their search of Ashmole 782 which takes them to Prague and John Dee's doorstep. What they learn in their quest is fascinating and Diana's inquisitive mind makes use of every morsel of information they gather.<br /><br />We also get to meet Matthews 'father', which you can imagine is a bittersweet moment for Matthew. While Diana tries to gain his father's respect, Matthew deals with his emotions in knowing what will happen to his father in the future. The reader gets a very clear picture of what life was like in the de Clermont household.<br /><br />I absolutely adored this book, as cumbersome as it was at times with the amount of characters and historical detail. Matthew gets more swoonworthy (as if that's possible!) and Diana grows more powerful and sure of herself. Even more exciting to me is that many of the events that take place in SON are real events in history, albeit with a fictional twist to the details and characters. More fascinating than that is that Matthew Roydon indeed was a real historical figure who was rumored to have been a spy for the Queen and indeed was in many of the locations that Matthew and Diana visit during that time in history. The history buff in me went hog wild researching after I finished, completely ensconced in learning more about the events and characters and utterly amazed that Harkness is able to weave such an intricate tale around real events in history. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14747937951682324143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_365548264" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/365548264" />
    <a title="Melinda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5002308-melinda"><img alt="Melinda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484434379p2/5002308.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/365548264?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melinda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melinda" href="/user/show/5002308-melinda">Melinda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5002308-melinda?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5002308-melinda?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer365548264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17488605112556852160">This book is an excellent follow up to A Discovery of Witches. I was afraid that the sequel would not live up to my expectations that have been building for a year since I read the first one. Luckily, that fear was incorrect.<br/><br/>Shadow of Night starts immediately where Discovery left off and begins to weave in various historical figures throughout the book right up until the end. In the first book there were many descriptions about the food and wine with great detail, in this one the detail is in th</span>
  <span id="freeText17488605112556852160" style="display:none">This book is an excellent follow up to A Discovery of Witches. I was afraid that the sequel would not live up to my expectations that have been building for a year since I read the first one. Luckily, that fear was incorrect.<br /><br />Shadow of Night starts immediately where Discovery left off and begins to weave in various historical figures throughout the book right up until the end. In the first book there were many descriptions about the food and wine with great detail, in this one the detail is in the historical aspects. I loved the historical features and characters in this book and felt that just as the descriptive food and wine gave the first book authenticity so did the historical features here.<br /><br />I loved getting glimpses of various historically famous places and people. Like any good book it made me want to go find out more. I have no doubt I will be reading about Christopher Marlowe and Walter Raleigh due to this book.<br /><br />The relationship between Matthew and Diana also did not disappoint. There was both romance and intrigue along with more secrets that hadn't been revealed before. There was enough suspense and action to keep my interest and balance out the romance.<br /><br />I loved this book, just as much as the first one. These are the only books I will own in both audio and Kindle version because the narrator is so amazing. I will be waiting on pins and needles for the third book. Undoubtedly it will go in my favorites shelf as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17488605112556852160" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer14988493137550853124">This book isn't great. <br/>It's too long.<br/>It's got some illogical thought processes from the main characters considering their supposed knowledge of all things historical.<br/>It reads like the author wanted to show off everything she knew about this time period.<br/>It's got far too many characters whose identities blur together.<br/>It's got some dodgy AF sexual interactions.<br/>And nothing much really happens despite the book's length.<br/><br/>But..... I give zero fucks about all of this because I had a blast. I am pure tras</span>
  <span id="freeText14988493137550853124" style="display:none">This book isn't great. <br>It's too long.<br>It's got some illogical thought processes from the main characters considering their supposed knowledge of all things historical.<br>It reads like the author wanted to show off everything she knew about this time period.<br>It's got far too many characters whose identities blur together.<br>It's got some dodgy AF sexual interactions.<br>And nothing much really happens despite the book's length.<br><br>But..... I give zero fucks about all of this because I had a blast. I am pure trash for this series so four stars it is <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380421555ra/837516.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<div id="review_3508244789" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3508244789" />
    <a title="Lucy Langford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford"><img alt="Lucy Langford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518091381p2/74034800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3508244789?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Langford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Langford" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford">Lucy Langford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780755384754" href="/book/show/17270883-shadow-of-night">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3508244789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17093357788187291550">2.5-3***<br/><br/><i>”You tell me that magic is just desire made real. Maybe spells are nothing more than words that you believe with all your heart.”</i><br/><br/>In this book Dianna and Matthew have timewalked to the year of 1590 in Oxford, England. Here they must search for the complete Ashmole 782. However, time walking has effects, and Dianna finds her magic playing up. <br/>Through this book we are able to see Dianna and Matthew’s search for Ashmole 782, the effects of the different time on their relationship, and Dianna</span>
  <span id="freeText17093357788187291550" style="display:none">2.5-3***<br /><br /><i>”You tell me that magic is just desire made real. Maybe spells are nothing more than words that you believe with all your heart.”</i><br /><br />In this book Dianna and Matthew have timewalked to the year of 1590 in Oxford, England. Here they must search for the complete Ashmole 782. However, time walking has effects, and Dianna finds her magic playing up. <br />Through this book we are able to see Dianna and Matthew’s search for Ashmole 782, the effects of the different time on their relationship, and Dianna taking control of some of her magic. <br /><br />Overall I found this book so unnecessarily long. So much of this was description of certain places during 1590, however, it’ll describe one thing to minute detail and move onto something else in minute detail, I just found myself getting so bored. I found the plot to this was also slow moving and some of the things that Matthew was involved with (so people he knew or jobs he had to do) just had me rolling my eyes. I also find that sometimes this book would mention highly intellectual or cultured topics and for someone like me, this could fly over my head or I just didn’t care. <br /><br />This definitely wasn’t action based or even magic based (which I really really wanted!). Most of the plot was just Matthew and Diana navigating their relationship... which just appeared so bleak on paper. I found their relationship and characters in this so much more one-dimensional and I got rather bored and annoyed at them. <br /><br />My favourite parts of this book were in the last 150 pages when we FINALLY get to see some things about Ashmole and see more magic and other witches. I really wish that the witches mentioned in this book were explored a lot more as their powers sounded so interesting and I was sad that this book had hardly any magic in it. This book does, however, include some questions that I do want answered.<br /><br />I can’t tell if this book just had “middle-book” syndrome and so I’m really questioning whether to carry on and finish the trilogy. While I didn’t hate this book it was super slow moving.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17093357788187291550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer373856499" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8870336787540039854">I had high hopes for this book after hearing about all the interesting places Diana Bishop (witch and historian) and Matthew (her vampire husband) would visit using time travel. Unfortunately, what resulted in between the hefty 600 pages, was a lot of frustration, boredom, and just a general feeling of "make it stop".<br/><br/>The Discovery of Witches, the first in the series, had so much potential but just ended up having too much of a resemblance to Twilight and too much irrelevant waffle. Shadow of Nig</span>
  <span id="freeText8870336787540039854" style="display:none">I had high hopes for this book after hearing about all the interesting places Diana Bishop (witch and historian) and Matthew (her vampire husband) would visit using time travel. Unfortunately, what resulted in between the hefty 600 pages, was a lot of frustration, boredom, and just a general feeling of "make it stop".<br /><br />The Discovery of Witches, the first in the series, had so much potential but just ended up having too much of a resemblance to Twilight and too much irrelevant waffle. Shadow of Night is even worse in that regard. While the Twilight veins have disappeared here, Shadow of Night not only capitalises on the worst frustrations of the first book, but adds its own as well.<br /><br />Where we left off in The Discovery of Witches was Diana and Matthew heading to the past to find a witchy tutor for her powers, and to uncover the Ashmore 982 manuscript.<br /><br />But when you pick up Shadow of Night, its best you forget where we were, the time travel elements, segregated world of witches, vampires and daemons, witch powers, and that snobby and possessive Matthew that you know (in other words, everything that was good about the novel). For you'll be thrust into the 16th Century with a bunch of historical characters and a bunch of new names that only history majors would recognise.<br /><br />Both Diana and Matthew are also strangely different in this novel, and for the worse as well. Diana's "daftness" and complete stubbornness to listen to anyone who makes sense (including Matthew who is only looking after her best interests) plagues the entire novel. Matthew's snobbery, distance, possessiveness and all of that are emphasised too. These people just refuse to listen to each other, which is probably why they are perfect(ly annoying) together.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2012/10/20/shadow-of-night-by-deborah-harkness-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">Continued on my blog here...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8870336787540039854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SNQJVPBHKS9tzQOrTxpsQiP0IleZhyPGrb2Vy+kB7mHBxgh2Q6NrPrZ3xI8Vekv27iXA+if5JMZWpHJE3FRQBw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lEOBccRwrUBznhpOP1W+TOBbYiNWBK7160vQcpv0HQMdUYBTd5TvUagk3WplNZn4LYqAjuh6qfUQUjf9rqGjZQ==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3849415.Deborah_Harkness">About Deborah Harkness</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3849415.Deborah_Harkness"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1584481459p3/3849415.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3849415.Deborah_Harkness">Deborah Harkness
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
24,110
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1712358778868763885">Deborah Harkness is a #1 New York Times bestselling author who draws on her expertise as an historian of science, medicine, and the history of the book to create rich narratives steeped in magical realism, historical curiosity, and deeply human questions about what it is that makes us who we are.<br/> <br/>The first book in Harkness’s beloved All Souls series, A Discovery of Witches, was an instant New York</span>
  <span id="freeText1712358778868763885" style="display:none">Deborah Harkness is a #1 New York Times bestselling author who draws on her expertise as an historian of science, medicine, and the history of the book to create rich narratives steeped in magical realism, historical curiosity, and deeply human questions about what it is that makes us who we are.<br /> <br />The first book in Harkness’s beloved All Souls series, A Discovery of Witches, was an instant New York Times bestseller and the series has since expanded with the addition of subsequent NYT bestsellers, Shadow of Night (2012), The Book of Life (2014), and Time’s Convert (2018), as well as the companion reader, The World of All Souls. The All Souls series has been translated in thirty-eight languages.<br /> <br />The popular television adaptation of A Discovery of Witches, starring Theresa Palmer and Matthew Goode, was released in 2019 by Sky/Sundance Now, and also broadcast on AMC. <br /> <br />Having spent more than a quarter of a century as a student and scholar of history, Harkness holds degrees from Mount Holyoke College, Northwestern University, and the University of California at Davis. She is currently a professor at the University of Southern California in Los Angeles, where she teaches European history and the history of science. <br /> <br />Harkness has published scholarly articles on topics such as the influence of theatrical conventions on the occult sciences, scientific households, female medical practice in early modern London, medical curiosity, and the influence of accounting practices on scientific record keeping. She has received Fulbright, Guggenheim, and National Humanities Center fellowships, and her most recent scholarly work is The Jewel House: Elizabethan London and the Scientific Revolution.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1712358778868763885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
